{"nick":"Sorella","message":"ozette: anyway, v8 does a lot of optimisations. When you run a program on v8, it starts by compiling your entire program to machine code, with some tracing symbols. It then runs that code on the processor. When it notices that a particular method has been called a lot, it takes that method and feeds into a second compiler, along with information it gathered","date":"2016-06-06T15:55:27.657Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"Sorella","message":"along this execution (which types it has seen, from where things have been called, etc), and this second compiler uses this information to generate really efficient code (removing redundant type checks because v8 already knows the type of something, inlining functions, and in some cases removing whole blocks of code because v8 doesn't need to execute them,","date":"2016-06-06T15:55:27.875Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"Sorella","message":"as it already knows the answer). If that optimised method is called even more, v8 moves it to a third compiler, which generates even faster code.","date":"2016-06-06T15:55:27.875Z","type":"message"}
